27/10/22, 7:12â€¯pm - #Ã§hÃ¤Ã±dÃ¡Ã±...: class Pattern2
{
    public static void main(String args[])
	{
		int i,j,k=1,l=1;
		for(i=1;i<6;i++)
		{
			for(j=1;j<=i;j++)
			{
				if(i%2==0)
				{
					System.out.print(k);
				}
				else
				{
					System.out.print(l);
					l--;
				}
				k++;
			}
			l=k+i;
			System.out.println();
		}
	}
}

	{

23/11/22, 10:26â€¯pm - #Ã§hÃ¤Ã±dÃ¡Ã±...: int n;
        cin>>n;
        int arr[n];
        for(int i=0;i<n;i++)
            cin>>arr[i];
        int low=0,high=n-1,count=0;
        while(low<high)
        {
            if(arr[low]==arr[high])
                low++,high--;
            else if(arr[low]>arr[high])
            {
                arr[low]=arr[low]-arr[high];
                high--;
                count++;
            }
            else
            {
                arr[high]=arr[high]-arr[low];
                low++;
                count++;
            }
        }
        cout<<count<<endl;
    }
	return 0;
23/11/22, 10:35â€¯pm - #Ã§hÃ¤Ã±dÃ¡Ã±...: int t;
    cin>>t;
    while(t--)
    {
        int n;
        cin>>n;
        int arr[n];
        for(int i=0;i<n;i++)
            cin>>arr[i];
        int low=0,high=n-1,count=0;
        while(low<high)
        {
            if(arr[low]==arr[high])
                low++,high--;
            else if(arr[low]>arr[high])
            {
                arr[low]=arr[low]-arr[high];
                high--;
                count++;
            }
            else
            {
                arr[high]=arr[high]-arr[low];
                low++;
                count++;
            }
        }
        cout<<count<<endl;
    }
	return 0;

09/01/23, 9:15â€¯pm - Priyanshu: import java.util.Scanner;

public class Pali {
    public static void main(String args[]) {
        int x, number, start, end, y, temp = 0;
        Scanner in = new Scanner(System.in);
        System.out.println("Enter The Range : ");
        start = in.nextInt();
        end = in.nextInt();
        for (number = start; number <= end; number++) {
            temp=0;
            y = number;
            while (number != 0) {
                x = number % 10;
                temp = temp * 10 + x;
                number = number / 10;
            }
            if (temp == y)
                System.out.print(y + "\t");
        }
    }
}

12/02/23, 10:41â€¯am - Priyanshu: Train a machine learning model to recognize the object: You can use a technique such as image recognition or object detection to train a machine learning model to recognize the object you want to track. The model can be trained using a dataset of images or videos of the object.
12/02/23, 10:41â€¯am - Priyanshu: this is ur part
12/02/23, 10:45â€¯am - Priyanshu: Training a machine learning model to recognize an object involves several steps:

Data collection: First, you need to gather a large dataset of images or videos of the object you want to track. This dataset should include a variety of images with different angles, lighting conditions, and backgrounds.

Data labeling: Next, you need to label the images in the dataset, so the model knows which images contain the object you want to track. This is typically done manually, by marking the object's location and class in each image.

Model selection: Choose a machine learning algorithm that is suitable for your problem, such as Convolutional Neural Networks (CNNs) for image recognition or object detection tasks.

Feature extraction: The model will need to extract features from the images in the dataset to recognize the object. This can be done using convolutional and pooling layers in a CNN.

Model training: Train the model on the labeled dataset. This involves feeding the images into the model and using an optimization algorithm to update the model's parameters so that it can accurately classify or detect the object in new images.

Model evaluation: Evaluate the model's performance on a separate validation dataset to determine how well it can recognize the object. If the model's performance is not satisfactory, you may need to make changes to the model architecture or collect additional training data.

Model deployment: Finally, use the trained model in your AR application to recognize the object in the camera feed and overlay AR content on top of it.

These are the high-level steps involved in training a machine learning model for object recognition. The specific details can vary depending on the machine learning algorithm and framework used.
12/02/23, 10:49â€¯am - Priyanshu: There are several technology stacks that can be used to train a machine learning model to recognize an object. Some of the most commonly used ones include:

Python: Python is a popular programming language for machine learning and has a number of libraries and frameworks available for building and training machine learning models. Some popular libraries for computer vision and machine learning include TensorFlow, Keras, OpenCV, and scikit-learn.

GPU hardware: Training machine learning models can be computationally intensive, so it's often necessary to use GPUs to speed up the process. Nvidia GPUs are commonly used for this purpose.

Cloud-based platforms: Cloud-based platforms such as AWS, Google Cloud, and Microsoft Azure provide access to powerful GPU instances for training machine learning models. They also offer pre-trained models and tools for deploying models at scale.

Development environments: Integrated development environments (IDEs) such as Jupyter Notebook and PyCharm can be used to write, test, and debug code for training machine learning models.

Datasets: You'll need a large dataset of images or videos of the object you want to track to train the model. There are many public datasets available, or you can create your own by collecting and labeling images or videos of the object.

These are some of the technology stacks that are commonly used for training machine learning models for object recognition. The exact tools and libraries used may depend on the specific problem and the resources available.

26/04/23, 11:10â€¯am - Priyanshu: #include <stdio.h>
#include <string.h>

#define d 256

void search(char pattern[], char text[], int q) {
    int M = strlen(pattern);
    int N = strlen(text);
    int i, j;
    int p = 0; // hash value for pattern
    int t = 0; // hash value for text
    int h = 1;
 
    // The value of h would be "pow(d, M-1)%q"
    for (i = 0; i < M - 1; i++) {
        h = (h * d) % q;
    }
 
    // Calculate the hash value of pattern and first window of text
    for (i = 0; i < M; i++) {
        p = (d * p + pattern[i]) % q;
        t = (d * t + text[i]) % q;
    }
 
    // Slide the pattern over text one by one
    for (i = 0; i <= N - M; i++) {
        // Check if the hash values of current window of text and pattern match
        if (p == t) {
            // Check for characters one by one
            for (j = 0; j < M; j++) {
                if (text[i+j] != pattern[j]) {
                    break;
                }
            }
 
            // If pattern is found at current position, print it
            if (j == M) {
                printf("Pattern found at index %d\n", i);
            }
        }
 
        // Calculate hash value for next window of text: Remove leading digit,
        // add trailing digit
        if (i < N - M) {
            t = (d * (t - text[i] * h) + text[i + M]) % q;
 
            // We might get negative value of t, converting it to positive
            if (t < 0) {
                t = (t + q);
            }
        }
    }
}
 
int main() {
    char text[] = "ABABDABACDABABCABAB";
    char pattern[] = "ABABCABAB";
    int q = 101; // A prime number
    search(pattern, text, q);
    return 0;
}

08/06/23, 5:49â€¯pm - #Ã§hÃ¤Ã±dÃ¡Ã±...: #include<bits/stdc++.h>
using namespace std;

int main()
{
    int ai,mth,daa,dbms,eco,os,daal,dbmsl,osl;
    float sgpa;
    cout<<"\n\n"<<"---WELCOME TO 4th SEMESTAR SGPA CALCULATOR---"<<endl;
    cout<<"---------------------------------------------"<<endl;
    cout<<"| Enter the corresonding Marks :-"<<endl;
    cout<<"|    AI : ";
    cin>>ai;
    cout<<"|    DBMS : ";
    cin>>dbms;
    cout<<"|    DAA : ";
    cin>>daa;
    cout<<"|    ECONOMICS : ";
    cin>>eco;
    cout<<"|    MATH : ";
    cin>>mth;
    cout<<"|    OS : ";
    cin>>os;
    cout<<"|    DBMS LAB : ";
    cin>>dbmsl;
    cout<<"|    DAA LAB : ";
    cin>>daal;
    cout<<"|    OS LAB : ";
    cin>>osl;
    
    sgpa=((dbms/10)+1)*4+((mth/10)+1)*4+((daa/10)+1)*4+((os/10)+1)*3+((eco/10)+1)*3+((ai/10)+1)*3+((daal/10)+1)+
    ((osl/10)+1)+((dbmsl/10)+1)*2;
    sgpa/=25;
    
    cout<<"| SGPA of 3rd SEMESTAR = "<<sgpa<<endl;
    cout<<"---------------------------------------------"<<endl;
    cout<<"------------------THANK YOU !----------------"<<endl<<endl<<endl;

    return 0;
}

16/06/23, 6:42â€¯am - Priyanshu: procedure BFS(start_vertex, adjacency_list):
    // Step 1: Create an empty queue and a boolean array visited[]
    queue = new Queue()
    visited = new BooleanArray(size_of_adjacency_list)

    // Step 2: Enqueue the starting vertex into the queue and mark it as visited
    queue.enqueue(start_vertex)
    visited[start_vertex] = true

    // Step 3: While the queue is not empty
    while queue is not empty:
        // Step 3a: Dequeue a vertex from the queue
        current_vertex = queue.dequeue()

        // Step 3b: Process the dequeued vertex (e.g., print it or perform any desired operation)
        process_vertex(current_vertex)

        // Step 3c: Enqueue all the adjacent vertices of the dequeued vertex that are not visited and mark them as visited
        for each adjacent_vertex in adjacency_list[current_vertex]:
            if visited[adjacent_vertex] is false:
                queue.enqueue(adjacent_vertex)
                visited[adjacent_vertex] = true

    // Step 4: Repeat steps 3 until the queue becomes empty

class HelloWorld {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
        System.out.println("\nEnter a Number : ");
        int num = sc.nextInt();
        if(num==0){
            System.out.println("\nNumber of digits : "+1); 
        }else if(num < 0){
               num = num * -1; 
               int dgts = (int)Math.log10(num) + 1;
               System.out.println("\nNumber of digits : "+dgts);  
        }else{
            int dgts = (int)Math.log10(num) + 1;
            System.out.println("\nNumber of digits : "+dgts);    
        }
    }
}

31/10/23, 10:42â€¯pm - Priyanshu: #include <iostream>
using namespace std;
int main()
{
    cout << "Enter The Outer Number : ";
    int n, num, i, j;
    cin >> num;
    n = 2 * num - 1;
    n -= 1;
    for (i = 0; i <= n; i++)
    {
        num = num + 1;
        for (j = 0; j <= n; j++)
        {
            if (j <= i)
            {
                cout << " " << --num << " ";
            }
            else if (j >= n - i - 1)
            {
                cout << " " << num++ << " ";
            }
            else
            {
                cout << " " << num << " ";
            }
        }
        cout << endl;
    }
}

29/01/24, 8:00â€¯pm - #Ã§hÃ¤Ã±dÃ¡Ã±...: Longest Common Prefix

Suppose you have been given an array consisting of n strings and you have found the string prefixes - which are the first i letters of each string. You are asked to find the length of the longest common prefix of all the strings in the array. Please write a program to find this out.

Input

The first line of input contains an integer n, representing the number of strings in the array. The second line of input contains an array of n space- separated strings consisting of lowercase English letters.

Constraints

The sum of lengths of strings does not exceed 105.

Output

Print the integer which is the length of the longest common prefix of all the strings.
29/01/24, 8:10â€¯pm - Priyanshu: int n = ar.size();
    if (n == 0) return 0;

    int minLen = INT_MAX;

    for (const auto& str : ar) {
        minLen = std::min(minLen, static_cast<int>(str.length()));
    }

    int commonPrefixLen = 0;

    for (int i = 0; i < minLen; ++i) {
        char currentChar = ar[0][i];

        for (int j = 1; j < n; ++j) {
            if (ar[j][i] != currentChar) {
                return commonPrefixLen;
            }
        }

        ++commonPrefixLen;
    }

    return commonPrefixLen;
